B003XKPPOU|5.0|Looking at the other two \\"Toy Story\\" movies, yes, there are definite repetitions, but \\"Toy Story 3\\" expands the story beautifully into emotional frontier many other animated sequels don't dare.     Every time a Pixar film comes out, the buzz is initially about how far off the deep end the animation studio has gone. \\"How can you make a movie about a dirty, filthy rat aspiring to be a gourmet chef without the film being the cinematic equivalent of an emetic?\\" \\"Seriously, a movie that begins in silence and a dead earth?\\" \\"A children's movie that touches on a miscarriage and old age mortality?\\"     My misgivings about \\"Toy Story 3\\" were far graver than those for \\"Ratatouille,\\" \\"Wall-E,\\" or \\"Up.\\" Instead of exploring bold emotional or aesthetic territory, it seemed that Pixar was treading into the familiar streets of Sequelville along with Dreamworks and Fox with their respective \\"Shrek\\" and \\"Ice Age\\" franchises.     The Monument Valley action opener was extremely amusing, but did not dispel my concerns as the sequence was very similar to the video game opening of \\"Toy Story 2.\\" Like the first two movies, Buzz the spaceman (voiced by Tim Allen), Woody the cowboy (Tom Hanks), Jessie the cowgirl (Joan Cusack), Hamm the piggybank (John Ratzenberger), Rex the dinosaur (Wallace Shawn), Mr and Mrs. Potatohead (Don Rickles and Estelle Harris), and Slinky Dog (Blake Clark filling in for Jim Varney) embark on an odyssey away from Andy (John Morris) where they meet new toys.     This time around Andy is grown up and heading off to college. He plans on taking Woody (more as a sentimental token than as a plaything) and leave the rest of the toys in the attic (something the toys consider to be a comfortable retirement). Through a mix-up and misunderstanding, they end up at a day care. What they initially take for a paradise, they find is really a prison run by a superficially friendly and menacing plush bear named Lotso (Ned Beatty) and a possibly more-than-metrosexual Ken doll (Michael Keaton). In the \\"caterpillar\\" room the gang is notoriously abused, their movable parts torn apart, bodies painted and glittered, body-parts crammed into every possible facial orifice.     The second act plays like a prison break film and in tone matches the other two films excellently. Like the other two films (or most other Pixar films) it displays a wonderful wit and all the characters new and recurring are in top comical form.     After the gang flees the day care, the film turns incredibly dark and dire. The movie explores obsolescence throughout, but in the last act the characters face death as they have not done before. The result is extremely gripping and affecting, whether as the result of a terrific build-up in a terrific movie or the result of spending 15 years and nearly five emotionally charged animated hours with Andy's toys.     The end runs a little too long beyond the climax, though not nearly as overlong as the denouement to \\"Lord of the Rings: Return of the King.\\" I mention \\"Return of the King,\\" because, like the third installment of that fantasy franchise, \\"Toy Story 3\\" attempts to find the happy medium between a conclusion to one movie and a conclusion to a trilogy.     All three \\"Toy Stories\\" work well singly or as one whole story. Pixar has pulled off its fourth absolute winner in a row (performing this feat, perhaps they can make me care about \\"Cars 2\\" next year). I would even venture to say that \\"Toy Story 3\\" belongs with other great cinematic sequels like \\"The Dark Knight,\\" \\"Return of the King,\\" \\"Aliens,\\" \\"The Empire Strikes Back,\\" possibly even \\"The Godfather: Part II,\\" all movies that effectively expanded and completed the story and themes begun in the movies they followed. \\"Toy Story 3\\" stands out from the rest of the pack of sequels as the only one that was able to do it with characters made of plastic.    As to the blu-ray as a package, I can't rightfully review, but my two favorite blu-ray review sites gave it superb scores in video and audio and supplements. For further reading, see  and . The only supplement I may comment intelligibly about is the short \\"Night and Day,\\" which, though I found the storytelling incredibly awesome (the mixture of 2-D and 3-D in theater worked excellently), I was nonplussed about some telling-not-showing toward the end and a pretty predictable arc. The best short in Pixar's post-Cars winning streak is easily \\"Presto.\\"

B000SEVVLK|3.0|Interestingly enough I LOVED this book when it came out a couple of years ago. BUT this weekend I couldn't find anything new I wanted to read to I figured I'd re-read a book I like the first time I read it, however, it seems I didn't figure on having matured since I read it last. I really didn't think I'd changed from when I was 24 to 26, but it seems somewhere along those years I matured without knowing it. It is the only reason I can think of to explain my change of mind regarding this book.  The first time I read it I felt just like the other reviewers who liked it. That it was funny and interesting, etc. Now, I can't believe that I actually liked it.   One character has what seems like the perfect life (a job she loves a promotion on the horizon and a sweet, handsome, famous, rich AND sensitive man who loves her) however, she is constantly whining about her life and even at one point thinking that she feels violated by her boyfriend's touch and having sex with him. YET, she still stays with him!!!    Another character is a serial monogamist who is devastated when her boyfriend of 5 years dumps her for younger woman. That of course doesn't seem like strange thing except the boyfriend was constantly cheating on her and according to one of her friends, always carried the card for his favorite escort service in his wallet. After being dumped and her friends succeeding in convincing her that having only had sex with 3 different men who were all boyfriends she decides to go on a Tour de Whore.     The last character is lacking in just that... character! She might be beautiful and she might rival the Victoria's Secret models in sexiness, however, she is so selfish and unconcerned with anything that doesn't revolve around her looks that I was left feeling that there's nothing there. The first two women I could scratch together a bit of sympathy with if I strained myself, however, the last one whores her way around New York and seems to think that is just dandy. She lives in her parent's apartment (but resents them for using it when they are in NY), she doesn't work, her parents pay all her bills and yet again she resents that her mother interferes in her spending ($10.000 for clothes and another $10.000 for travel in one month is apparently not any of their business). While I am not a prude (Sam in SATC is my favorite character! But unlike this character she had a job and a life she'd made for herself instead of mooching of off her family!!!), the simple fact that she sleeps with married men without any thought made me actively dislike her, all the other stuff is just added on to my dislike.    I am 26, yet I feel WAY more mature than these three women!!! How am I supposed to relate to them when there is nothing there?! They never seemed to have left their teenage years behind!    I've given it 3 stars because I did love it the first time I read it.
030745455X|5.0|Lisbeth Salander is in Grenada.  A woman in the next hotel room is being abused, slapped around.  Mikael Blomkvist, a journalist, had been surprised by Salander's odd talents.<br /><br />This is the second in a sort of trilogy, (the late author planned to produce more than the three books published to date).  Lisbeth's adventures in the first book created enemies.  One, in this episode, joins forces with some of the officials who are seeking to find the cause of three unexplained deaths.<br /><br />Prior to that point, Blomkvist learns, during a weekly planning meeting at the magazine, MILLENNIUM, that Erika Berger, the editor, is inclined to have one themed issue focus on trafficking.  A freelance journalist has a book and an article to offer to the magazine.  Blomkvist is to be the editor of the book.<br /><br />This is a wonderful piece of fiction.  The reader is immediately caught up in the travails of the girl.  The deep appeal of all three books in the series is that it is something of a Cinderella story, even a superman story, for that matter.  Lisbeth Salander is a true underdog, someone whose gifts are not properly valued, who prevails against a veritable mountain of obstacles to survive.  Most people are not positioned as far outside of the human community as she is, but everyone, in some small way,  has been put in humiliating circumstances, bested unfairly, felt alienated, been misunderstood, and so forth.  There is universal capacity to identify with such a heroine.<br /><br />The author has produced an interesting, multifaceted mysterious plot of excitement, charm, and bite to dazzle the reader.  Throughout much of the book the journalists and Lisbeth are operating on separate but linked tracks.  A number of strands to the story are pitched and then converge.  Each line of inquiry is interesting in and of itself.  This is a cliff hanger.
